### Post by Iowan on 2013-05-29
> **Irihapeti said:**
> I'll ask another question, of our staff: what else are we allowed to talk about here?Well, what would you LIKE to talk about?  Staff has a similar area where we discuss forum policy, weekend plans, and theme days (noticed the camels lately?) My opinion might (or not) agree with other admins, but I would envision this forum similar to the IRC channel. Support questions? Ideally, these would go in a support forum, but there are times when you might prefer a more select group. 
Unofficially, (meaning I didn't really type this) the Ubuntu Forums Members Area might include topics that would be closed elsewhere - AirCrack, etc. I think our Ubuntu Forums Members have earned a **little** leeway. If a topic gets offensive, it can still be reported/closed. The CoC still applies.

---

### Post by Irihapeti on 2013-05-29
Well, on the other forum (support.toastmastersclubs.org, if anyone is curious) – and tell me if you get sick of me saying that – we mods occasionally blow off steam about users who've got under their skin. All quite polite and no bad language. Mention gets made of policies we are meant to follow when answering a question, and posting style in general. Sometimes, it's "I had x situation in my club. Any of you guys had something similar, and what did you do and what do you recommend?"

On that forum, promotion to mod status is rare, so you don't need to worry much about someone getting promoted and then seeing the horrid things we said about him/her. :oops: Whereas here one would need to be a lot more circumspect and restrict it to "what do you think/do when people do x in a post?"

I might have the occasional support question that I'd rather not ask in the main forums, for fear that I'd get jumped on by the haters. But then, maybe I'm just a bit too sensitive.

### Post by CharlesA on 2013-06-30
Double bump for finally getting my SMART script fixed (and rewritten)

Old:

```
#!/bin/bash

###
### smart.sh
### Script to check SMART on all drives
### Created by Charles Auer
### Tested 03/20/2011
### Updated 03/20/2011
###

# Path Variables
BIN=/bin/
USR=/usr/bin/
SBIN=/sbin/
USBIN=/usr/sbin/
HOME=/home/charles/
LOGS=${HOME}logs/smart/
# Filename variables
RES="results"
MON="smartmon"

MON1=${LOGS}${MON}1
MON2=${LOGS}${MON}2
MON3=${LOGS}${MON}3
MON4=${LOGS}${MON}4
MON5=${LOGS}${MON}5
MON6=${LOGS}${MON}6
RES1=${LOGS}${RES}1
RES2=${LOGS}${RES}2
RES3=${LOGS}${RES}3
RES4=${LOGS}${RES}4
RES5=${LOGS}${RES}5
RES6=${LOGS}${RES}6
# Email variable
EMAIL=user@domain
# Text variables
OS="OS Drive"
RAID1="RAID Drive 1"
RAID2="RAID Drive 2"
RAID3="RAID Drive 3"
RAID4="RAID Drive 4"
DAILY="Daily Backup Drive"
# The "Find RAID array device" variable
RAID="$(fdisk -l | grep 4294967295 | cut -c 1-8)"
# Date variable
DATE=$(${BIN}date +%m-%d-%y)


# SMART check OS Drive
echo $OS > ${MON1} && ${USBIN}smartctl -a /dev/sda >> ${MON1}
echo -e $OS > ${RES1}
${BIN}grep -e result ${MON1} | awk -F' ' '{print $1"\t\t\t"$6}' >> ${RES1}
${BIN}grep -e Power_On_Hours ${MON1} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t\t" $10}' >> ${RES1}
${BIN}grep -e Reallocated_Sector_Ct -e Reallocated_Event_Count -e Current_Pending_Sector -e Offline_Uncorrectable ${MON1} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t" $10}' >> ${RES1}
echo -e "" >> ${RES1}

# SMART check RAID Drive 1
echo $RAID1 > ${MON2} && ${USBIN}smartctl -a -d hpt,1/1 $RAID >> ${MON2}
echo -e $RAID1 > ${RES2}
${BIN}grep -e result ${MON2} | awk -F' ' '{print $1"\t\t\t"$6}' >> ${RES2}
${BIN}grep -e Power_On_Hours ${MON2} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t\t" $10}' >> ${RES2}
${BIN}grep -e Reallocated_Sector_Ct -e Reallocated_Event_Count -e Current_Pending_Sector -e Offline_Uncorrectable ${MON2} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t" $10}' >> ${RES2}
echo -e "" >> ${RES2}

# SMART check RAID Drive 2
echo $RAID2 > ${MON3} && ${USBIN}smartctl -a -d hpt,1/2 $RAID >> ${MON3}
echo -e $RAID2 > ${RES3}
${BIN}grep -e result ${MON3} | awk -F' ' '{print $1"\t\t\t"$6}' >> ${RES3}
${BIN}grep -e Power_On_Hours ${MON3} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t\t" $10}' >> ${RES3}
${BIN}grep -e Reallocated_Sector_Ct -e Reallocated_Event_Count -e Current_Pending_Sector -e Offline_Uncorrectable ${MON3} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t" $10}' >> ${RES3}
echo -e "" >> ${RES3}

# SMART chceck RAID Drive 3
echo $RAID3 > ${MON4} && ${USBIN}smartctl -a -d hpt,1/3 $RAID >> ${MON4}
echo -e $RAID3 > ${RES4}
${BIN}grep -e result ${MON4} | awk -F' ' '{print $1"\t\t\t"$6}' >> ${RES4}
${BIN}grep -e Power_On_Hours ${MON4} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t\t" $10}' >> ${RES4}
${BIN}grep -e Reallocated_Sector_Ct -e Reallocated_Event_Count -e Current_Pending_Sector -e Offline_Uncorrectable ${MON4} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t" $10}' >> ${RES4}
echo -e "" >> ${RES4}

# SMART chceck RAID Drive 4
echo $RAID4 > ${MON5} && ${USBIN}smartctl -a -d hpt,1/4 $RAID >> ${MON5}
echo -e $RAID4 > ${RES5}
${BIN}grep -e result ${MON5} | awk -F' ' '{print $1"\t\t\t"$6}' >> ${RES5}
${BIN}grep -e Power_On_Hours ${MON5} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t\t" $10}' >> ${RES5}
${BIN}grep -e Reallocated_Sector_Ct -e Reallocated_Event_Count -e Current_Pending_Sector -e Offline_Uncorrectable ${MON5} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t" $10}' >> ${RES5}
echo -e "" >> ${RES5}

# SMART check Daily Backup Drive
DAILY=$(${SBIN}blkid /dev/sd?? | ${BIN}grep Daily | ${USR}cut -c1-8)
echo $DAILY > ${MON6} && ${USBIN}smartctl -a $DAILY >> ${MON6}
${BIN}grep -e result ${MON6} | awk -F' ' '{print $1"\t\t\t"$6}' >> ${RES6}
${BIN}grep -e Power_On_Hours ${MON6} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t\t" $10}' >> ${RES6}
${BIN}grep -e Reallocated_Sector_Ct -e Reallocated_Event_Count -e Current_Pending_Sector -e Offline_Uncorrectable ${MON6} | awk -F' ' '{print $2"\t" $10}' >> ${RES6}

${BIN}cat ${LOGS}result* > ${LOGS}summary
${BIN}cat ${LOGS}smartmon? > ${LOGS}smart_$DATE.log
${BIN}rm ${LOGS}result* ${LOGS}smartmon*
sed -i 's/_/ /g' ${LOGS}summary
${BIN}cat ${LOGS}summary | ${USR}mail -s "SMART Status `${BIN}date +%D`" $EMAIL
${BIN}rm ${LOGS}summary
# eof

```

New:

```

#!/bin/bash

# Standard Variables
date=/bin/date
smartctl=/usr/sbin/smartctl
pvs=/sbin/pvs
grep=/bin/grep
cut=/usr/bin/cut
blkid=/sbin/blkid
mail=/usr/bin/mail
egrep=/bin/egrep



# Other Variables
# Find device name of OS drive (LVM)
os=$($pvs | $grep Thor | $cut -c 3-10)
# Find device name of RAID drive (LVM)
raid=$($pvs | $grep raid | $cut -c 3-10)
# Find device name of external drive (Daily Backup - non-LVM)
daily=$($blkid -c /dev/null | $grep Daily | $cut -c 1-8)
# Get MM-DD-YYYY for email subject
longdate=$($date +%m-%d-%Y)

# Log Variables
log=/home/charles/logs/smart/smart_$longdate.txt
summary=/tmp/summary_$longdate.txt

# Use tee to copy the entire output before filtering
tee="/usr/bin/tee -a $log"

# egrep string
string='(Model)|(Serial)|(Firmware)|(User)|(Size)|(RAW_VALUE)|(Raw_Read_Error_Rate)|(Throughput_Performance)|(Spin_Up_Time)|(Start_Stop_Count)|(Reallocated_Sector_Ct)|(Seek_Error_Rate)|(Seek_Time_Performance)|(Power_On_Hours)|(Spin_Retry_Count)|(Power_Cycle_Count)|(Runtime_Bad_Block)|(End-to-End_Error)|(Reported_Uncorrect)|(Command_Timeout)|(High_Fly_Writes)|(Airflow_Temperature_Cel)|(G-Sense_Error_Rate)|(Power-Off_Retract_Count)|(Load_Cycle_Count)|(Temperature_Celsius)|(Reallocated_Event_Count)|(Current_Pending_Sector)|(Offline_Uncorrectable)|(UDMA_CRC_Error_Count)|(Hardware_ECC_Recovered)|(Current_Pending_Sector)|(Offline_Uncorrectable)|(UDMA_CRC_Error_Count)|(Head_Flying_Hours)|(Total_LBAs)'

# Email Variable
email=user@domain

# Set timestamp
$date | /usr/bin/tee $log > $summary
echo "" | $tee >> $summary

# Check OS drive
echo "OS Drive" | $tee >> $summary
$smartctl -a $os | $tee | egrep $string >> $summary
# Add space
echo "" >> $summary

# Check RAID Drive 1
echo "Raid Drive 1" | $tee >> $summary
$smartctl -a -d hpt,1/1 $raid | $tee | $egrep $string >> $summary
echo "" >> $summary

# Check RAID Drive 2
echo "Raid Drive 2" | $tee >> $summary
$smartctl -a -d hpt,1/2 $raid | $tee | $egrep $string >> $summary
echo "" >> $summary

# Check RAID Drive 3
echo "Raid Drive 3" | $tee >> $summary
$smartctl -a -d hpt,1/3 $raid | $tee | $egrep $string >> $summary
echo "" >> $summary

# Check RAID Drive 4
echo "Raid Drive 4" | $tee >> $summary
$smartctl -a -d hpt,1/4 $raid | $tee | $egrep $string >> $summary
echo "" >> $summary

# Check Backup Drive
echo "Daily Backup Drive" | $tee >> $summary
$smartctl -a $daily | $tee | $egrep $string >> $summary

# Mail the log
$mail -s "Smart Status $longdate" $email < $summary

```

### Post by sffvba[e0rt on 2013-12-26
> **CharlesA said:**

---

### Post by cariboo on 2014-02-12
You can't see the house from that picture, that's the tool shed, garage and storage shelter. We got rid of the wood stove years ago, as it added to the already huge amount of fly-ash that came from the 6 sawmills that were here at the time. A couple have closed since, and all the wood waste is now trucked to a electric co-generation plant that manages to capture the fly-ash before it is released into the atmosphere.

---

### Post by Bashing-om on 2014-02-12
cariboo907;

That sounds like you are "down home" !
Environmentally friendly is a good thing for sure, but, how are you managing to keep warm in that "extreme" environment ?

a bump for "down home"

---

### Post by cariboo on 2014-02-12
> **Bashing-om said:**
> cariboo907;

That sounds like you are "down home" !
Environmentally friendly is a good thing for sure, but, how are you managing to keep warm in that "extreme" environment ?

a bump for "down home"

We only have two cold spells a year where the temps go down to -30°C (-22°F) or lower, the rest of the time average temps are in the 5°C (41°F) to -10°C (14°F) range this is a fairly dry area, where the humidity is rarely above 70%. We use natural gas for heat, and seeing as British Columbia is an exporter of gas, prices are fairly reasonable.

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-02-16
Blow in the cat's nose when you put the pill in it's mouth. It causes them to swallow. Drop the pill or capsule as far back over the tongue as possible, then immediately close the mouth and blow on the cat's nose which will encourage it to swallow.

### Post by Bashing-om on 2014-02-26
Me do internet BumP too !
Lost my connection Sunday Morning too, all me installs on this box.. after a lot of fixes I am just now back up on my primary preferred system (about 30 minutes past). -Pulled out my backup box, no will boot ! -
It has been a struggle, and a lot of the fixing was just plumb magic. I detest when things just fix themselves. 
switched out the ethernet card
Bent pin on the original ethernet card (when ??)
Mac not recognized by the router (re cloned )
corrupted file on my "work" install

Got the internet up and working on the 12.04 installed system, then the 13.04 Lubuntu was working, no workie in my "work" install... hummm !
Believe it or not a sound troubleshooting procedure is a good thing . I found my /etc/network/interface file corrupted (step 3).
Copied over the file from Lubuntu install, rebooted, and to my amazement and utter delight -> those 5 dots appeared rather than the horrid 4 dots !

[INDENT][INDENT]wonderful thing

---

### Post by cariboo on 2014-03-03
It all really depends on who you are creating the POS for, is it for a Mom and Pop corner grocery store, a small chain store, or a major retail chain, they all have different needs.

The Mom and Pop store can be a little harder to use, as there is just a small number of people that will be using it, the small chain should be set up with ease of use in mind, and maybe some form of transaction storage, so that it can communicate with the main server at the end of the day. The major retail chain system should be designed with ease of use in mind, as staff turn over is usually fairly high, so training cost should be kept in mind, this type of system is typically run as terminals connected directly to a server.

---

### Post by CharlesA on 2014-03-03

Haven't seen one of those for something like 40 years. Gosh, I'm beginning to feel old!.

We used a Gestetner Mimeograph machine to produce the school newspaper. We used several IBM [selectric]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_Selectric_typewriter") typewriters to produce the stencils.

This was all in the time period when Easy Rider (the movie), Woodstock (the movie) were released and Jimi Hendrix passed away (real life). 

So I guess that makes me one of the old on the outside, as [s]forestpixie[/s] Elfy said in another thread. :-P

Used them as a first and second year Biology student, yes, we had to take Fortran classes.
Then the first PDP 11/23 hit the lab when I was a PhD student. Got to write handlers with an electronic engineer to control a microscope :)

Bump. Ah, a picture of the important END card. I remember the problems that were caused by someone forgetting it. :)

Edit: FYI, punch card decoder...
```
     ______________________________________________
    /&-0123456789ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQR/STUVWXYZ
 Y / x           xxxxxxxxx
 X|   x                   xxxxxxxxx
 0|    x                           xxxxxxxxx
 1|     x        x        x        x
 2|      x        x        x        x
 3|       x        x        x        x
 4|        x        x        x        x
 5|         x        x        x        x
 6|          x        x        x        x
 7|           x        x        x        x
 8|            x        x        x        x
 9|             x        x        x        x
  |________________________________________________

```

We watched the movie on her laptop screen. It was sooo interesting that I can't remember what it was or what it was about. :)

Anyway, I decided to boot Window 7 Home Premium, and update it for the next time. When it loaded, I checked for updates and found I had not updated since I retired from my real-life job over a year ago. I guess I didn't need Windows until now. I spent the next 2 1/2 hours babysitting the computer while it updated and rebooting. I used my notebook for surfing the web while I waited.

I need to put a calendar entry that reminds me to update Windows every 3 months.

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-04-29
@Bashing-om

Bump, and it continued moving eastward. I am thankful I have never had my home destroyed by one of those things.

When I was younger and physically able I went to areas hit by tornadoes. Sometimes all I could do was stack bricks, remove nails from lumber, and stack the lumber for them to use to rebuild. The pictures you see on TV and the Internet don't show how surreal it actually is. Tornadoes can do some really strange things.

---

### Post by Bashing-om on 2014-04-29
@ Old_Grey_Wolf; Yeh,

Three towns around us have been hit ( more than once each !), and the cleanup is never completed, and what was lost is not replaceable. A building(s) might get rebuilt, but it is not the same as the memory of what was.  The only good thing one, who has been in a tornado, can say is that they say anything at all. Many lives are lost. 

You put it really well, pull nails, stack and bull doze and sweep - as a community effort - and none of it seems real. Gotta sweep even before the trucks can get in to start cleaning up. The clean up goes on and on and on, and no one forgets and all do what and as much as they can to overcome. 

[INDENT][/INDENT]On the effort of so many, a town arises anew.

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-05-09
I saw that the "Ubuntu Members Only Bump Thread" had been dead for 3 or 4 days. I wanted to stimulate the thread. The "Ubuntu Members Only Bump Thread" is a means for communication between forum staff and forum members. It is not just changes in the forum or forum rules that get communicated. There is also the subtle indication of cultural changes that are taking place that get communicated as well. Sometimes joking tells a lot about the culture.

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-05-12
Bump!

Here we go again. It has been less than a week. Flash flood, high wind, thunder storm, and hail watches all over the area. I am glad there are no tornado watches or warnings this time. 

I need to tell my neighbor that their roof drainage system is stopped up with leaves. Their roof looks like a waterfall. 

The high and low temperatures are going to drop 20[sup]o[/sup]F over night. As an older person, I was enjoying that the temperature was starting to get warm enough for me to be comfortable. :)

No, I have lived here for 60 years, and know this is not that unusual.

Boom! that was loud and a spectacular flash. Well if I loose power, I have an LED flashlight in one pocket and a fully charged cell phone in the other. 

:lolflag:

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-05-26
> **lisati said:**
> LOL! I was feeling lazy and couldn't be bothered typing "Digital." ...

I remember they called their computers PDP, then they changed the architecture and called them VAX, and finally changed the architecture again and called them DEC. I programmed the PDP 11/05 using the front panel toggle switches, then used the VAX 3100 through 7600, and finally the DEC ES40. It is funny the things you remember. I can't remember the names of most of the people I worked with. LOL.

---

### Post by bapoumba on 2014-05-27

PDP 11/23, first human sized computer that ever hit the lab when I was a PhD student. Fun times, he would experiment left and right writing handlers and I had to kill him on a regular basis from our local network. First Unix encounter ever, guess I got formatted properly :)

The code the team developed was run on Linux boxes. In 2011 the company decided to upgrade everyone from XP to Windows 7 and the new Microsoft Office with the ribbon. It took about a year to accomplish due to the size of the company. An upgrade to Windows 8.1 or whatever follows would be fun to watch. :)

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-07-22
Bump for funny things that happen. 

When my wife and I both worked I was paying to have my laundry done. Since I retired I have been washing my own clothes. First it is less expensive and second the clothes last longer. I probably hadn't washed my own clothes in 40 years. 

It fascinates me that I can take off my long sleeve shirts, and the sleeves are *not* inside-out; however, after washing and drying them, at least one shirt out of every load has a sleeve that is inside-out. Why, How? And where do the buttons go? Well, at least I don't have a problem with missing socks that fall into a black hole, just the buttons. :)

### Post by Elfy on 2014-09-04
> and now I can't really be considered as an Ubuntu Member as I don't contribute >.< (which got me thinking, should I even have access to this sub-forum?) You gained membership to the Forum Ubuntu Members group for your contributions - the contributions that you made haven't disappeared overnight. You'll get - as everyone does - a mail eventually telling you that you're due to expire and allowing you to continue to have Ubuntu Member status. 

Once membership is gained it's not removed except for exceptional circumstances and as far as I am aware that is the responsibility of the Community Council.

So as a member of the team which gave you Ubuntu Member status - do you want me to jail your post :)

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-09-13
> **lisati said:**
> ...My surname is rare here in New Zealand...

Bump.

My two letter surname **was** rare here in the USA a decade ago; however, we now have a lot of immigrants from Asia where it is more common. My ancestors are from Germany. They had lived there for about 350 years as far as I can tell from Hugenotten (Huguenot) birth and marriage records. The surname is not that common in Germany either, about 250 telephone listings the last time I checked. Since they were Hugenotten (Huguenot) they may have originally come from France in the 1650's to 1670's; however, I have not been able to confirm that.

### Post by Bashing-om on 2014-09-20
Bumb !

Though non 'buntu related, I think well deserves a feel good bump .

Got started on the Winter's fire wood this day.
Long story, that makes me feel the better. That old mossy back hickory was leaning heavily over the daughter's house and a high dollar chainlink fence;
That sucker was 38 inches in diameter, and my saw has a 20" blade. Now I had had spent considerable time and thought on how to get that tree down and this day saw the successful completion of the thought process .
Cut down with the aid of my son-in-law pulling the rope tied to the top. I made the 3 cuts up on the trunk of the tree where I could be sure the blade would penetrate on that 4th cut as he pulled mightily on the rope. Over she went - perfect in all respects ! Did not jump back into the fence, did not pin me, or roll over me, did not jam the saw into me .. Prior prudent planning !

It has now been cut down to the ground, blocked up, split up and hauled to the wood shed. 1/4 of our wood is now in the dry.


[INDENT][INDENT]all in how you do it
[/INDENT][/INDENT]

---

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2014-09-20
When I was 14 or 15 years old, I helped my father clear some trees on lake property so we could build a house. We were careful to plan it out so no one ever got hurt. The worst thing that happened was when I climbed a tree on a hot humid day in shorts and no shirt in order to tie the rope in it. After we cut it down we saw that it was covered in [Poison Ivy]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toxicodendron_radicans") vines. I was miserable for weeks. :lol:

### Post by cortman on 2014-09-23
Thanks y'all! Funny how I got started on it.
I like doing MOOCs through the edX platform, and saw recently that they were offering a course on Linux (LFS101x), so I signed up for it. On the big opening day I looked at the material and laughed. Rather than do any of the homework or watch any videos, I went straight to the final exam, which took about 3 minutes and I got 100% on (it was REALLY basic).
Couple weeks later I got an email from the Linux Foundation saying as one of the early finishers of LFS101x they were offering me a 50% discount off the LFCS or LFCE exams. I decided to go for LFCS to get my feet wet. The IT manager at my job said that if I got the cert he could use some help managing the fileservers here, so it looked like a good opportunity.

I've got a handfult of tapes like that gathering dust somewhere, recorded in the late 1980s during a Doctor Who 25th (?) anniversary special. A preliminary run through with the William Hartnell tape went without major hassles, even though there were signs of mould/dust/something on the tape.

I've got other priorities at the moment, such as getting some of the in-laws family memories on to DVD. Some of the tapes they provided are in a dodgy condition - not rewound properly, damaged in places, dust and other muck on the tape - so I've reverted to using my own copies where possible. One advantage is that mine are in better condition, and since I recorded many of them in the first place, they're one step closer to the quality of the long-since reused original camera tape.

Bump and
why the heck I cannot login via ssh in people.ubuntu.com ? 
It just hangs without any errors (tried with -v -v for vverbose output). 

```

debug2: channel 0: request shell confirm 1
debug2: callback done
debug2: channel 0: open confirm rwindow 0 rmax 32768
debug2: channel_input_status_confirm: type 99 id 0
debug2: PTY allocation request accepted on channel 0
debug2: channel 0: rcvd adjust 2097152
debug2: channel_input_status_confirm: type 99 id 0
debug2: shell request accepted on channel 0

```

I can connect without issues via sftp (or graphical file manager or filezilla), but not with ssh directly. Any ideas? 

The only I can think is the different versions of ssh between local and remote, but I don't know if that matters, I guess it doesn't, because sftp uses ssh also in order to connect.

---

### Post by NikTh on 2014-10-27
Bump for probably figured out what's going on. There is no need for "pure" SSH connection to administer something. 
I can connect without problems via SFTP, but in SSH just hangs. So, I cannot think of any different (right now).

---

### Post by CharlesA on 2014-10-27
sftp calls the sftp subsystem instead of trying to login into the shell. Have you tried using a different user?

---

[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PeopleUbuntuCom](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PeopleUbuntuCom)

> All [Ubuntu Members]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Membership") who have signed the Code of Conduct are granted **SFTP** access to a Web-accessible directory on people.ubuntu.com.

### Post by uRock on 2014-11-12
> **Old_Grey_Wolf said:**
> Bump.

We also get more ice than snow. I have about 4 lbs. of de-icer for the stairs and walkway. That doesn't mean I can drive anywhere; but, I can at least get my trash bins to the curb without falling down. :lol:

Freezing rain is destructive. When the power goes out and all you hear is trees breaking apart in the distance. When I was a teen in Virginia, we got three inches of solid ice from the freezing rain. The grass was still green when it came down, so when we went outside it was like walking on a sheet of glass with 3D foliage within it. 

Here's a HowTo for making "snow chains" for your shoes. [http://www.backpacker.com/view/photos/survival-photos/make-snow-traction-with-bungee-cord/#bp=0/img1](http://www.backpacker.com/view/photos/survival-photos/make-snow-traction-with-bungee-cord/#bp=0/img1)

```
/*
	Compute the number of cubic inches
	in 1 BUMP.
*/
class Inches {
	public static void main(String args[]) {
		long ci;
		long im;
		
		im = 5280 * 12;
		
		ci = im * im * im;
		
		System.out.println("There are " + ci + " cubic inches in a BUMP.");
	}
}
```

### Post by MAFoElffen on 2014-12-04
bump.

I was NCO, then OCS. Only needed 2 years of college for that. Got out as a Captain. I would have needed 2 more years of college to get oak leaves. They offered to send me, but I didn't want to owe them 5 more years. But then I got hurt, so that answered that for me.

It was at a time when I thought I needed to do something else. Looking back, I should have got my 4 years degree then. Now the VA is paying me to go back to college and am in class with very few my age. I tell my wife that she can tells her friends she's with a college kid...

### Post by MAFoElffen on 2014-12-05
Funny thing was that when I came out of the service, getting a job in IT, everyone was fine taking experience. I had experience people wanted. But in the PC world in the early nineties, you wore many hats. But then it started specializing.

I was young and stupid and decided I'd rather do construction. I kept up with my IT skills as a consultant. Now that I'm older and my body is more beat up, I can sit behind a desk. But getting back into IT full time, I was being told that I had plenty of experience, but that I did not have any degrees or certifications. Since I live in a state capital, I was competing with people who had Masters. Now collecting degrees and certifications. Computer Programming, Database Management, Software Engineering. I start testing for my certs this spring... Web Design, Oracle Java Certs, A+, N+, Cisco CCENT...

### Post by Irihapeti on 2015-02-25
There's another name that gets used in a similar way: Eketahuna.

This one is a real place, population < 500, in the lower North Island. For a while some years ago, I used to drive through it twice a week.

It's the butt of various jokes, which if I repeated here, would get me an infraction. :)

---

### Post by QIII on 2015-03-19
"Smog"

---

### Post by cariboo on 2015-03-19
We have two plants in the Williams Lake river valley that produce huge amount of steam, enough that the climate in the valley has changed for the worse during the winter. The extra humidity makes temps feel much colder then they are once you leave the valley. I'd call that pollution fog.

---

### Post by bapoumba on 2015-03-20
Fog : clouds that stay on the ground. basically made of water drops.
Pollution fog (or smog as QIII said ?) : chemicals and small particles that stay on the ground due to high pressures and no wind. Basically made of poison.

I live by the sea, wind is almost always blowing. I saw a pic of the fog coverage in France : one third of Northern part of the country.. Never saw that in my entire life. Your pics are accurate Frogs Hair, same here :(

---

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2015-08-08
This is an old joke and used in various versions in the south west of the US:

May 30th:

Just moved to Dallas. Now this is a city that knows how to live!! Beautiful sunny days and warm balmy evenings. What a place! I watched the sunset from a park lying on a blanket. It was beautiful. I've finally found my home. I love it here.

June 14th:

Really heating up. Got to 100 today. Not a problem. Live in an air-conditioned home, drive an air-conditioned car. What a pleasure to see the sun everyday like this. I'm turning into a sun worshiper.

June 30th:

Had the backyard landscaped with western plants today. Lots of cactus and rocks. What a breeze to maintain. No more mowing lawn for me. Another scorcher today, but I love it here.

July 10th:

The temperature hasn't been below 100 all week. How do people get used to this kind of heat? At least it's kind of windy though. But getting used to the heat and humidity is taking longer that I expected.

July 15th:

Fell asleep by the pool. (Got 3rd degree burns over 60% of my body). Missed 3 days of work. What a dumb thing to do. I learned my lesson though. Got to respect the ol' sun in a climate like this.

July 20th:

I missed Morgan (our cat) sneaking into the car when I left this morning. By the time I got to the hot car for lunch, Morgan had died and swollen up to the size of a shopping bag and stank up the $2,000 leather upholstery. I told the kids that she ran away. The car now smells like Kibbles and shits. I learned my lesson though. No more pets in this heat.

July 25th:

The wind sucks. It feels like a giant freaking blow dryer!! And it's hot as hell. The home air-conditioner is not working and the AC repairman charged $200 just to drive by and tell me he needed to order parts.

July 30th:

Been sleeping outside by the pool for 3 nights now. $1,500 in damn house payments and we can't even go inside. Why did I ever come here?

Aug. 4th:

It's 115 degrees. Finally got the air-conditioner fixed today. It cost $500 and gets the temperature down to 85, but this freaking humidity makes the house feel like it's about 95. Stupid repairman. I hate this stupid city.

Aug. 8th:

If another wise ass asks, "Hot enough for you today?" I'm going to strangle him. Damn heat. By the time I get to work the radiator is boiling over, my clothes are soaking wet, and I smell like baked cat!!

Aug. 9th:

Tried to run some errands after work. Wore shorts, and sat on the black leather seats in the ol' car. I thought my ass was on fire. I lost 2 layers of flesh and all the hair on the back of my legs and ass. Now my car smells like burnt hair, fried ass, and baked cat.

Aug. 10th:

The weather report might as well be a damn recording. Hot and sunny. Hot and sunny. Hot and sunny. It's been too hot to do **** for 2 damn months and the weatherman says it might really warm up next week. Doesn't it ever rain in this damn desert? Water rationing now, so my $1700 worth of cactus just dried up and blew into the damn pool. Even the cactus can't live in this damn heat.

Aug. 14th:

Welcome to HELL!!! Temperature got to 115 today. Forgot to crack the window and blew the damn windshield out of the car. The installer came to fix it and said, "Hot enough for you today?" My wife had to spend the $1500 house payment to bail me out of jail. Freaking Texas. What kind of a sick demented idiot would want to live here?

---

### Post by Bashing-om on 2015-12-21
BumP;

For MucH faster booting !

A bit back disconnected my box and cleaned all the dust out and also the fans, well .. seems I lost my bios settings .
I reset my bios settings to sane settings .. and now I boot 3 times as fast as it has up to this time .
I boot to grub in about 2 seconds - wow ! From a cold boot !!

No, do not go looking for a LAN connection - I do not do that anymore
no, do not look for a 3.5 inch drive A - does not exist
no, do not do a floppy seek, no such thing installed either
No, do not go looking for a CD to boot up
no, I am only going to boot from hard drive(s)
no, Ram is fine, no need to verify

Yeah, maybe a couple of tweaks on how memory is handled

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-01-17
BumP;

Sweat condition 10 is ended.

Backup hard drive with ATA errors swamping the system and logs !
Somehow or other I did a no-no in making my weekly backups this morning - no idia of why the bad command I ran caused the partition table to corrupt ... but but ...

finally I spared of the superblock and 

[INDENT][INDENT][INDENT]all is well

### Post by Irihapeti on 2016-01-17

---

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-01-17
Irihapeti; Uh Huh !

Had me going for a few hours . Maybe just co-incidental ... I do not see how a invalid target directory copy attempt to the valid destination ( my backup drive) could have crashed the partition table(s) ... 

Sure drove the system nuts ... could not even boot up a liveDVD !

Was finally able to boot up my work install through grub in all the error reports ... and was able to run a ' touch /forcefsck ' on the main drive ... reboot and able to get to to a GUI and activate a terminal. - errors generated to TTY1 , so could work the GUI - From there "smartctl" just puked on a long test ..
forget trying to run 'fdisk' for that hard drive ... uh uh ! 'blkid ? Uh UH ---
Wow ... what in the world ? SATA controller gone haywire ? Hard drive crashed ... What in the world ??

fsck just hung up for the longest ... Just about the time I gave up on fsck I got meaningful output !
Took fsck's hint and spared off the superblock ... fsck'd a lot of yeses ... and YES ... I could then mount the partition when fsck was all done with the new superblock.

Redo once again my backup ... All looks to be hunky dory at the present time/

BumP

[INDENT][INDENT][INDENT]how do you spell relief ?
[/INDENT][/INDENT][/INDENT]

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-02-05
BumP;

Restoration of internet service .

It is absolutely amazing the creature of habit that we are.

Semi-truck hung a low hanging line across the hyway, ripped out the cables, fiber optics and snapped off the power pole(s), pulled others over ! Energy power folks were fast on the scene and quickly had the truck released and power secured; reopening the road.
We had our services for internet, phone and TV restored that same evening .. with the warning was but a patch job . Full repair as time allowed and additional checks reveal the complete condition of the damage done.

[INDENT][INDENT]wow survived a whole day with out
[INDENT][INDENT][INDENT]what we can endure when there is no other choice

### Post by Irihapeti on 2016-02-20
I can't say that the situation with Discourse surprises me. I visit it regularly, and I notice it's been almost dead for quite a while.

Unfortunately (and this is somewhat off-topic re NikTh's question), almost inevitably, the question of "why do we need the forums?" has come up at the same time. Maybe it would be helpful if we had a response worked out ahead of time, instead of just reacting when pushed into a corner.

One obvious answer is that maybe the forums gives people something that other venues don't. Having spent a bit of time lurking on various StackExchange sites, I get seriously fed up with the amount of time and energy that goes into arguing about whether a question should even be asked. I can ask a question here and, as long as I abide by the Code of Conduct, I'm very unlikely to be told that it's inappropriate, get it downvoted etc.

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-03-21
BumP !

How do you spell relief !

Hard drive restored and back in service, file system reclaimed ( mostly ) .. and appears what I am missing is in the lost+found directory.
Replaced sata cable(s) ( locking !)
Moved to a different sata port on the controller
Spared off the super block on the partition X2
3rd attempt with e2fsck was the charm

This on my backup drive - 5+ years of data, and upon 'lookin' not complete ! --- Where is all my programming stuff ??? My system restore directory ?? They used to be there !  hummm what have I done - NOT ! - . Most else is backup backed up .

A progression from a non-booting system, to booting up screaming of hardware errors, booting up with file system errors.

Booting now and all is hunky dory, and I can rebuild . And do a better job of backing up my backups . Lesson learned .

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-05-24
BumP;

For an un-OUCH!

Hot swapping hard drives and in a moment of thoughtless-ness , in-consideration ( as it turned out) I had removed my booted operating system hard drive ! Ouch !!
Took me a bit to realize why applications were crashing and my log files were running amuck .. and on a reboot attempt .. bios was real unhappy !

Hard power down ( yuk ! ) because well .. the system would not accept keyboard inputs to power down in any form ! 

Connected the correct drive
reset bios to boot the proper device
boot up the system
set to run a file system check on next reboot
reboot
fire up the system. activating applications - some still unhappy with how they had been treated !
restart the apps

Bump for the Un-ouch ; All appears good now.

[INDENT][INDENT]haste makes waste
[/INDENT][/INDENT]

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-10-15
Bump;

Mods completed on this ole box - nVidia GT 710 card replacing the old ATI card .. and a 256 Gig SSD.
All finally coming up roses but was an adventure finding out that the card is so new that in 14.04 there is no open source support for it.

Bump for sounding like fun! I did a reinstall yesterday. It would've been uneventful if I hadn't followed the advice given when adding the Truecrypt repo. ```
To automatically grant TrueCrypt root privileges to mount volumes, run:
sudo nano -f /etc/sudoers.d/truecrypt
And put the following in the file:
your_username ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:/usr/bin/truecrypt
```All was good until I dropped out of sudo su, then try to run another sudo command.

After trying and failing to drop into recovery mode to delete the file, I ended up booting into a LiveUSB and elevating nautilus to delete it.

---

### Post by Bashing-om on 2016-12-21

for pressing on .. and the accumen to fix.

> Bump for sounding like fun! I did a reinstall yesterday. It would've been uneventful if I hadn't followed the advice given when adding the Truecrypt repo. ```
To automatically grant TrueCrypt root privileges to mount volumes, run:
sudo nano -f /etc/sudoers.d/truecrypt
And put the following in the file:

> 
-a, -b, -e, -f, -g, -j

whatever was in the originators mind ?

### Post by Irihapeti on 2017-07-20
Actually, I don't recall any general derision or RTFM on these forums at all. Or sexism for that matter. Well, OK, the occasional troglodyte, but they got put in their place very quickly.

When I started, I had only dialup, which initially didn't work on Ubuntu. My first posts were about a package getting stuck in a half-installed state - probably nothing I'd done wrong but a little tricky to fix. Fortunately, I got the help I needed, and promptly.

I just wish I had some area of expertise that I could share with the users. Most of the stuff I play with is rather arcane and of limited interest (e.g. my custom-built router). Apart from that, everything "just works" and I'd have no idea what to do with things such as wireless, graphics, audio and so on. These days, my main job seems to be hitting spammers on the head. :)

---

### Post by oldos2er on 2017-07-20
> **chili555 said:**
> That was very common on forums when I started in Linux way, way back in 2001. 

Hoo boy. In the mid-90s the comp.os.linux.* newsgroups were rife with RTFM, flames, insults and elitism out the wazoo. Occasionally you read some helpful posts, but you were expected to know so much before you could even be considered a noob. $DEITY help you if you dared to complain about being flamed. Mostly I read the comp.os.os2.* groups though, which were slightly more welcoming.

Good times.

### Post by Bashing-om on 2017-07-20
Bumpit;

On the plus side - call it a maturing operating system perhaps .
I came up in computers with open source 70's 80ish - usenet;  tried Windows - did not like ! . Messed about with several linux distros . Groussed at all of em . File server running slackware - What a pain . A friend introduced me to (k)ubuntu for the desktop , I found my way to (u)buntu .
Was relieved at the level of documentation that was available and then I found this forum !
Been 'buntu'n ever since .
Lurked about the forum for a spell - learned bunches ! .
Found I could answer to a few issues and had ample help in discovering solutions to issues over my head here on this forum .
All I can say is the forum and the people frequenting and supporting it made my road a lot less bumpy. And made the ride a pleasure .

Fairly straight forward with a multi-meter to isolate the faults - source power ( blown fuse ??), thermostats, heating element , wires . All there is to it :)

[INDENT][INDENT]even a cave man can do it
[/INDENT][/INDENT]

---

### Post by lisati on 2017-10-01
> **Bashing-om said:**
> lisati; Lies, lies !!



They just want your money .

Fairly straight forward with a multi-meter to isolate the faults - source power ( blown fuse ??), thermostats, heating element , wires . All there is to it :)

[INDENT][INDENT]even a cave man can do it
[/INDENT][/INDENT]
As near as I can make out, it has something to do with the ripple control/load management box on the meter board, which I can't reset myself, at least not legally. It's not the first time it has unexpectedly stayed in the "off" position, and it has was replaced a year or two back.

---

### Post by jeremy31 on 2017-10-01

[INDENT][INDENT]even a cave man can do it

Bump for basic electrical safety and a vote for a bad heating element or 2
I use a propane fired water heater and haven't had an issue in 15 years

So I take it that the electricity provider has some control over when the water heater is used?

---

### Post by lisati on 2017-10-01
> **jeremy31 said:**
> So I take it that the electricity provider has some control over when the water heater is used?

There's a sealed "ripple control" box on our meter board which the electricity people use to manage supply to hot water cylinders during times of peak use, it has been showing "Off" since yesterday morning. 

No sign of the regular circuit breaker having been tripped.

The results of an experiment involving a nail, wire, and electrical outlet when I was little taught me to proceed with caution with anything beyond a basic visual safety check.

It's just a name. I was tired of the length of my Xbox gamertag of CabooseLinux. (Caboose885 was taken) On a whim one night I decided to start change my name. So I smashed Kirby and Caboose together. That's great news! I hope your eyes heal up and everything is good with them. :)

My mum had surgery for cataracts and she had some complications where the swelling didn't want to go down and her vision didn't want to clear up like it was supposed to. It turned out that she had something called "Fuchs’ Dystrophy", which required her to get a cornea transplant in both eyes to restore her version.

I probably have the same disorder in my eyes, but it won't manifest for a few decades. I'm just glad to have clear vision (even if I need to wear glasses!)

### Post by QIII on 2021-06-28
Bump for 95°F/35°C at 25% humidity at 10:00am here on the farm.  Forecast is for 115°/46° and < 10% humidity at 5:00pm.  

In case that doesn't seem hot to you, I live in the Pacific Northwest of the US.  These temperatures are unheard of around here.

Our well water is about 55°/13° year round, so I went out and hosed down the alpacas a few minutes ago.  They love that.  They are a high altitude/low temperature animal that can normally tolerate PNW temperatures, but they are hot right now.  The goats and chickens don't seem to be terribly stressed.  Goats and chickens don't like to get wet anyway.

The dogs zip outside to relieve themselves and run right back in.

The old farmer in his 60s is just sitting at his desk in the A/C doing his normal paid work developing software and neglecting the farm chores.

Oy!

---

### Post by CharlesA on 2021-06-28

That's just nuts for that area.

---

### Post by QIII on 2021-06-28
We didn't have an A/C unit at our first house when we moved to the area 20+ years ago.  Didn't need it and didn't miss it.

We bought a new house later.  It didn't have A/C either.  No need.

Third house, no A/C to begin with, but we put it in because it had started to get a lot hotter.

This place an A/C unit for the farmhouse was a requirement for our purchase.

Our neighbor to the north doesn't have A/C and they are hating it.  Most rural homes in our county don't have it.  It was just not needed 10 or 15 years ago.

---

### Post by CharlesA on 2022-02-10
Bump for trying to figure out why I am getting a crash due to "out of space" on my backup server.

zfs list showed 2TB of free space, but df -h showed I had 2M of free space. Bugger.

Now I need to figure out what I want to do - get a set of 8 x 18TB drives to replace the drives in my main server and move the main server drives to the backup server or just add a couple 18TB drives to the backup server, move files around and proceed as usual until I've got enough cash to upgrade everything.

So far I've found a deal at western digital for a pair of gold drives for 600 dollars and that's the cheapest price I've found so far. Only problem limit 2 per customer and I would need 8 of them. :lolflag:

### Post by Irihapeti on 2022-02-17
Backups?

Oh, wait, it was the backup server....

(Does one backup the backup server? Must admit, I don't.)

---

### Post by CharlesA on 2022-02-17
> **Irihapeti said:**
> Backups?

Oh, wait, it was the backup server....

(Does one backup the backup server? Must admit, I don't.)

That's a good question...

I do not back the backup server up, but I have separate backups stored on a bunch of different drives that I could restore from if/when the primary backups on the backup server are bad.

It's backups all the way down!

At least it's not hugely expensive to do it this way, since I replace the backup disks when I upgrade the disks in my main server, and then use the disks from the backup server as secondary/tertiary backups.

### Post by CharlesA on 2022-03-26
Bump for playing the data shuffle while trying to update some backups so they use a newer hash algorithm. Unfortunately, this means I need to extract the original backup archives and recreate them in a new repository with the updated hash.

This becomes a problem when you have a 33TB archive for bluray rips and you don't have enough space to hold the whole thing. I'm probably going to end up using a bunch of drives in RAID 10 to try to cobble together enough space to do this.

### Post by Bashing-om on 2022-08-26
Bump

as I must show the hand:

18.04 -> 20.04 login loop
fsck: said system was in consistent state
/mnt : respective partitions and all data intact
Full Chroot: Make grub boot menu available
root terminal from Grub: Hey the system is alive - but on the old old kernel
user terminal from grub: apt tells me to do the dpkg thing for the inconsistency things
user terminal from grub: apt now to finish updates/cleanup
20.04: Boots and appears all good on correct kernel version
20.04: execute do-release-upgrade
22.04: \o/

[INDENT]just goes to prove that it can be done

BumP[/INDENT]

### Post by QIII on 2023-02-23
Bump for going out at 03:45 (US West coast) to check on the livestock.  24°F/-5°C.   10"/25cm+ of snow in the last 5 hours and still coming down hard.  Windy as heck.  Everyone was just lounging around under the feed shelter, chewing cud and whatnot.

The animals are fine.  The old farmer in his 60s, on the other hand, is gumpy after getting up twice in the middle of the night to go out in the foul weather to check on them.  Not as bad as out on the ranch in Eastern Montana in the winter at -30°F, but pretty nasty for NW Oregon.

### Post by QIII on 2023-02-24
3:30am again.  13F/-10C.  Still 12"/30cm of snow.  No wind.  The critters are just haging out doing their thing.  Alpacas naturally have exceptionally good insulating fiber.  The goats grew their undercoat of cashmere and they are fluffy.  

This is as cold as we have seen it since we moved to Oregon, so I wasn't sure how it was going to go.

### Post by lisati on 2024-01-25
> **Irihapeti said:**
> Bump for the trains are back in force.

(I live close to a commuter rail line and the trains have been out of service for nearly a month while they did maintenance/repairs/upgrades. Occasionally I get to see steam trains, which is fun.)

BUMP for the trains in my area being out of action several times lately. One of the projects is the replacement of some signalling equipment that was installed in the 1930s. Another project is the addition of a third platform at another station,  which also required modifications to the signalling system. 

And yes, I do get to see steam trains every now and again. Here's a link to a clip of one such encounter, one end was a stem locomotive,  the other a vintage diesel. [https://youtu.be/ZohP_gc8kh4?si=YCAIQ844EcimdhPR]("https://youtu.be/ZohP_gc8kh4?si=YCAIQ844EcimdhPR")
